text:
I made this for my grown son's birthday (cake) - it was a huge hit.  When we lived in San Diego, we used to get the most delicious flan.  Back in our hometown in the Midwest, I wanted to make a great flan, and this was excellent.  Made it exactly like the recipe - 3 eggs only, and I poured the custard mixture through a sieve into the baking dish.  When making the caramel, I used 1 C sugar + a generous "squirt" of fresh lemon juice.  Heated slowly over medium heat - NO stirring!!  When liquid, poured into a warm glass baking dish and swirled to cover the bottom.  Before baking, I covered with foil, put in a large roasting pan, added hot water 1/2 way up the baking dish.  Baked for one hour, cooled, then refrigerated.  Couldn't have been more perfect.  Silky smooth and just delicious!  Absolutely rivals any I've ever had!

text:
After reading the reviews I did several things differently.

I used the microwave method of carmelizing the sugar which was perfect and I would not consider doing it any other way.  I put 1 cup of sugar in a pyrex measuring dish and added ¬Ω cup of water, stirred the water and sugar, and then microwaved.  Initially high power for 4 min, Stirred once with a wooden spoon, then 2 min increments (no more stirring) until golden brown/amber color.  Took about 8 minutes.  I had the ramekins sitting in a pan in warm water and then poured in the sugar and swirled to coat the bottoms and a little of the sides.

I used the blender to mix the ingredients.  I put the eggs in first and blended them, then added everything else.  Worked great, well mixed.   Very easy to pour into the ramekins from the blender.  This recipe was enough for 8 ramekins.

My big conundrum was about how long I should bake the flan.  In the reviews the baking times ranged from 30 minutes to 2 hours.  I initially baked 30 minutes then added 10 minutes then added about 5 minutes twice.  So I think ultimately baked it for about 50 minutes.  I think that was a little long.  The flan tasted great and was nice and firm, but I think could have been a little creamier if baked a little less time. So, maybe 40-45 minutes would be better next time.  Some reviewers said it should be a little jiggly in the center when you take it out of the oven. Mine was not.  Others said the knife should come out clean, my toothpick never did,

text:
As flans go, this is a good recipe.  I did add more eggs (2) which made it a bit eggy, so maybe better to keep with 3 eggs.  As far as making the caramel, I do agree with a reviewer that recommended adding water just enough to cover the sugar and have it look like sand.  This is how the professionals do it.  But, be sure not to stir it because if sugar gets on the sides of the pot it crystallizes.  So, put in sugar in the middle of the pot, spread it out a bit, then add some water.  Poke it with a knife or such to get all the sugar under water.  Follow instructions of letting the sugar boil at the lowest heat possible without stirring it and watch for the color to change.  Once it starts turning color, you can ensure even color by swirling the liquid in a circular motion just by moving the pot in a circular motion.  Let it get a solid amber color, be patient.  I didn't warm the ramekins as one suggested, wasn't necessary.  Just spooned in the caramel and tilted the ramekins immediately to have it settle evenly.  Not really a big issue because when you warm the ramekin later the sugar (more instructions forgotten in the recipe) will liquify and allow you to invert it onto a plate.  Even though I used individual sized ramekins, it still took 60 minutes for the custard to cook so that there was just a small jiggle in the middle.  I did place the ramekins on a thin towel inside a roasting pan and filled the roasting pan with hot water up mid-way on the ramekin.  This may have mad

city:

None
country:
None
text:
My advice is:
1. Preheat along with water bath at 350F and lower it to 320F once you put in the custard bowl to bake. 
2. To make it creamy use half and half or heavy cream. Also, use more egg yolks more than whole eggs. 
3. Use small baking dish; preferably ramekins or tea cups
4. I use granulate sugar rather condense milk for less to remember to buy. 
5. Make sure to strain through sieve to make it less bubbles and more creamy smooth consistency.
6. Don't use blender at all for making too much foam and bubbles that cause "holes" inside your flan.
7. Use toothpick (insert and out should be clean) to check rather just shaking the flan at the end of baking to cause less water bath spillage.

This was so awesome. Perfect recipe. I did use the water bath like some of the reviews suggested.
I'm not sure how how adding water to the sugar was supposed to help, but it only made rock candy for me. Not caramel!! Its much easier to add the sugar to a pot and put it on med high and watch it.  It gets brown pretty quickly.  You can swirl it around or give it a quick stir and take it off of the eye. That works for me. 
I also strained the mixture through a fine colander into the bowl. Thank God because there were a few egg lumps.

It came out so smooth, creamy, and sweet. It was the perfect consistency. I covered ot tightly and put it in the fridge to cool.

text:
I've used this recipe before, I loved it then as well. 
this time, instead of soiling a pan to make caramel (which is too much trouble to clean, in my experience) I oiled the pyrex dish and put the sugar straight in! I placed it under the broiler of my oven for about 15 minutes. checking on it every 5 minutes. the indirect heat of the oven is much easier to make the caramel- directly in the dish. once the sugar looks 80% melted and golden brown, take it out. so it doesn't burn. then add the custard. you'll thank me later ;) enjoy!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
i tried this in the pressure cooker.  I glazed the Carmel mixture in Unheated custard cups, poured the mixture in and sealed with aluminum foil.  I did not blend the mixture in a blender, just whisked it.  I did add an extra half cup of milk to it.  I have a six quart pressure cooker, and placed the custard cups on the rack in the cooker.  Once the pressure rocker began to rock, cooked it for 10 minutes.  Then I immediately cooled it under running water and set the cups to  cool until they were able to be handled.  Then I inverted  each one into a serving bowl.  They came out perfect, but because I didn't invert them immediately, wasn't as much syrup.  I have larger custard cups so could only do it in batches, two at a time, but I think for the smaller ones may be easier to glaze too..  I used 1 cup of water in the cooker.

text:
This is a family favorite.  Rock your world good.  Impress all your latin friends and make this for them.  I made it exactly how it was written and it's awesome.  I've also taken suggestions of using 1 extra egg and that works too.  In addition, if you're not a fan of caramelizing sugar in a pan, use the microwave!  It works, it's fast, and (almost) error free.  I have to warn you though, don't burn the sugar... you'll regret it, stink up your place, and probably set off alarms.  As an alternative suggestion, you can also mix an 8 oz. package of cream cheese into the mix if you want that brick in your belly feeling (a richer flan).  Flan fans.  Take not.  Try this.  It really is a five star recipe.

My only additional notes on this recipe are, 1) when melting the sugar, make sure the bottom of your saucepan is nice and wide so that your sugar makes as thin a layer as possible. That way, it won't be burned by the time it's all melted. Also, on my stove, medium heat for melting the sugar was plenty. =) 2) MAKE SURE TO BAKE COVERED. It loses too much moisture if you don't!

I never thought of flan as something that I could make myself. I would order it at a local resturaunt, which is awesome, but expensive. Overall, this is a good recipe and very, very easy! I did the water bath like other people suggested and the texture was wonderful (placing the smaller pan in a larger pan and pouring boiling hot water into the larger pan until it reaches the midpoint of the small pan to bake). I really do like this recipe, although I thought 1 tablespoon of vanilla was overkill. I think next time I will half it. Also, just a dash of cinnamon would be nice in the sauce. text:
I used 3 jumbo eggs, probably would equal 4 large.  I made the custard in a blender first, so it'd be ready to pour into the pie plate.  Also knew exactly how much water was needed for the water bath and had that boiling.  Someone mentioned crystalizing the sugar in the pie plate in the microwave, so I did that.  1 cup of sugar, 1/4 cup of water and a few drops of lemon juice. It was easy.  @6 minutes.  I did it at 2-minute intervals and watched it.  As soon as it turned light brown, I put the pie plate in a roaster, poured the custard on top, then the boiling water and into the oven.  Refrigerated it overnight and crossed fingers when I turned it onto a plate.  It turned out great.  Compliments from my card club.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Amazingly simple recipe, provided you add a few tweaks. When you are making your caramel, wait until it starts to melt. When it starts to get that rich almost amber color, take it off the heat and toss in a couple of pads of butter. It'll cool the caramel down so it doesn't over cook, mix until the butter is all or almost gone (it will melt quickly), then pour into your mold. I had a Pyrex glass pan that I put a washtowel on the bottom off, flat, and water so it would reach half of my flan mold once the mold settled to the bottom. Then, cover with tin foil and cook. It took me an extra 20 minutes, but it came out very creamy, rich and not too egg-ey. Added an extra egg and about a teaspoon of vanilla extract to the recipe. Will be making again. I used La Lechera brand condensed milk and it seems to do the trick well.

text:
The first time I prepared flan dish from this recipe, the flan did not come out right. The caramel was too liquidy, even after I allowed it to set over night. When I checked the flan the following morning, the caramel was still liquidy and the custard part of the dish was darkened on top. I followed the recipe exactly the way it stated but was not satisfied. I highly recommend placing a glass pan of water beneath flan dish prior to cooking(did not specify in recipe) to give it that beautiful color and texture. The second time I prepared this dish, I place a pan of water beneath it, and it came out great.

Thank you for this recipe!  It is very simple (compared to the others posted), even I could make it without messing up! I made a few alterations to make it a 'little' healthier and reduce the # of calories. I used 5 eggs as suggested by a reviewer and the texture was still nice. I used low fat milk instead of evaporated milk but the same amount per the recipe. and I did not use the entire can of condense milk - i used 3/4 just to cut back on some calories lol but it was still sweet enough for my liking. I omitted the caramel part because i did not feel adventurous and i am not missing the added sugar.  Can't wait to eat the rest this afternnon and make some more next week!

text:
1. Use a DEEP dish  pie pan, not the regular size.  I had egg mixture left over and got a FLAT flan.  2.  I forgot to cover it with aluminum foil and I don't know if that's what made the flan so "cakey" but I love a very custardy flan, so this didn't work for me.   Maybe the 5 eggs I used caused it?  3. When baking in a bath, use a cookie sheet with sides, and boil the water and pour it into the cookie sheet AFTER your flan is placed and ready to put in the oven. (no one tells you that.  I put the water in while I was preheating both pans which made handling them drippy and way too hot and dangerous while trying to pour the egg mixture).  Duh.  4, My guests thought this was tasty, but it was too cake like for me.  Very nice flavor however.  But not the texture I remember from Spain.
